Read thisFirst:
The rules of this SPI simulation game are organized in a
format known as rhe Case Slsterr. This system of
organization divides the rules into Major.gectmar (each of
which d€als wilh an important aspect of play). These Sec-
tions are fiimb€rsd sequentially as well as being named.
Each of these Major Sections h introduced by a Car€rdl
Rtl/e, Irhich briefly describes the subject of the Section.
Many times th;s ceneral Rule is followed by a P/ocrdtr?
which describes 
the basic action the Play€r will take when
using lhe rules in that Section. Finally, th€ bulk of each
Major Section consists of Carar. These are the specific,
detailed rules that actually regulale play. Each of these
Cases is also numbered. The numbering follows a logical
system based upon the number of the Major Section of
which the Cases are a part. A Case with the number 6.5,
for example, is the fifth Primary Cd.re of the sixrh Major
Section of the rules. Many times these Primary Cases are
further subdivided inlo Seconddrt Cdser. A Secondary
Case is recognizable 
by the fact that il has two digirs ro the
righl of its decimal point. Each MajorSection can have as
many as nine Primary Cases and each Primary Case can
have as many as nine Secondary Cases. The numbering
system is meant as an organizational aid. Using it, Players
can always easily tell where a Case is located in the rules.
As a further aid, an outline of the Major Seclions and
Primary Cases is given at the beginning ofthe rules.

How to Learn to Play the Game:
Familiarize yourself with all of the components. Read all
of theGeneral Rules and Procedur€sand read the titles of
lhePrimary Cases. Set up thegame for play (afierreading
lhe pertinent Section) and play a trial game against
yourself referring to the rules only when you have a ques-
tion. This proc€dure may take you a few hours, bul it is
the fastest and most entertaining way to learn the rules
short of having a friend teach them to you. You should
not attempt to learn the rules word-for-word. Memorizing
all that detailis a task ofwhich few ofus are caoable. SPI
rules are wrilten to be as complele as possible - they're
not designed to be memorized. The Case numbering
rysrem males il eesy to look up rules when you are in
doubt. Absorbing the rules in this manner (as you play) is
a much better approach togame mastery than attempting
to study them as ifcramming for a tesr.
We hope you enjoy this SPI game. Should you have any
difficulty interpreting the rules, please wrire 10 SPI,
phrasing your questions so that th€y can be answered by a
simple sentence, word, or number. Yoo must enclose a
slamped, self-addressed 
envelope. We cannot guarantee a
proper answer should you choose to phone in your ques-
tion (the right person is not always available - and since
SPI haspublished hundreds ofgames, no oneindividual is
capable ofanswering all qu€stions). Write ro:
